<p><b>Andrew McLean "Drew" Galloway IV</b> (born 6 June 1985)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-facebook.com_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-facebook.com-1">[1]</a></sup> is a Scottish <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling" title="Professional wrestling">professional wrestler</a> currently signed with <a href="/wiki/Total_Nonstop_Action_Wrestling" title="Total Nonstop Action Wrestling">Total Nonstop Action Wrestling</a> (TNA), where he is a <a href="/wiki/List_of_TNA_World_Heavyweight_Champions" title="List of TNA World Heavyweight Champions">one-time</a> <a href="/wiki/TNA_World_Heavyweight_Championship" title="TNA World Heavyweight Championship">TNA World Heavyweight Champion</a> and a one-time <a href="/wiki/Impact_Grand_Championship" title="Impact Grand Championship">Impact Grand Champion</a>. Galloway is perhaps best known for his tenure with <a href="/wiki/WWE" title="WWE">WWE</a>, where he performed under the <a href="/wiki/Ring_name" title="Ring name">ring name</a> <b>Drew McIntyre</b>. He has also worked extensively with many independent wrestling promotions, including <a href="/wiki/Insane_Championship_Wrestling" title="Insane Championship Wrestling">Insane Championship Wrestling</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Evolve_Wrestling" title="Evolve Wrestling">Evolve Wrestling</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pro_Wrestling_Guerrilla" title="Pro Wrestling Guerrilla">Pro Wrestling Guerrilla</a>, and WhatCulture Pro Wrestling (WCPW), for whom he is the current WCPW World Champion in his first reign.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>While with WWE, he held their <a href="/wiki/WWE_Intercontinental_Championship" title="WWE Intercontinental Championship">Intercontinental</a> and <a href="/wiki/WWE_Raw_Tag_Team_Championship" title="WWE Raw Tag Team Championship">WWE Tag Team Championship</a> once each, as well as winning the <a href="/wiki/FCW_Florida_Heavyweight_Championship" title="FCW Florida Heavyweight Championship">FCW Florida Heavyweight Championship</a> and <a href="/wiki/FCW_Florida_Tag_Team_Championship" title="FCW Florida Tag Team Championship">FCW Florida Tag Team Championship</a> on two occasions for their (pre-<a href="/wiki/WWE_NXT" title="WWE NXT">NXT</a>) developmental brand <a href="/wiki/Florida_Championship_Wrestling" title="Florida Championship Wrestling">Florida Championship Wrestling</a> (FCW). Outside of WWE, he has held numerous other titles both on the <a href="/wiki/Independent_circuit" title="Independent circuit">independent circuit</a> and internationally. He is a multi-time <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling_championship#World_championships" title="Professional wrestling championship">world champion</a>, having held the TNA World Heavyweight Championship once<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-8">[8]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/ICW_World_Heavyweight_Championship_(Scotland)" title="ICW World Heavyweight Championship (Scotland)">ICW World Heavyweight Championship</a> <a href="/wiki/ICW_World_Heavyweight_Championship_(Scotland)#Reigns" title="ICW World Heavyweight Championship (Scotland)">twice</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> Galloway also held the <a href="/wiki/Evolve_Championship" title="Evolve Championship">Evolve Championship</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DGUSA_Open_the_Freedom_Gate_Championship" title="DGUSA Open the Freedom Gate Championship">DGUSA Open the Freedom Gate Championship</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Evolve_Tag_Team_Championship" title="Evolve Tag Team Championship">Evolve Tag Team Championship</a> with <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Gargano" title="Johnny Gargano">Johnny Gargano</a>. Under Galloway, both the ICW and Evolve Championships were renamed world championships due to numerous international defenses as champion.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Professional_wrestling_career">Professional wrestling career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Drew_Galloway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Professional wrestling career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Galloway began training for professional wrestling at the age of 15<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slambio_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-slambio-2">[2]</a></sup> at the <a href="/wiki/Frontier_Wrestling_Alliance" title="Frontier Wrestling Alliance">Frontier Wrestling Alliance</a>'s Academy when his family moved to the south of <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a> to <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth" title="Portsmouth">Portsmouth</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-record_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-record-10">[10]</a></sup> In the FWA Academy, while he was trained by the promotion's operator <a href="/wiki/Mark_Sloan_(wrestler)" title="Mark Sloan (wrestler)">Mark Sloan</a> along with Justin Richards and <a href="/wiki/James_Tighe" title="James Tighe">James Tighe</a>, Galloway also cites the promotion's established wrestlers helping out with training, including <a href="/wiki/Doug_Williams_(wrestler)" title="Doug Williams (wrestler)">Doug Williams</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Burchill" title="Paul Burchill">Paul Burchill</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alex_Shane" title="Alex Shane">Alex Shane</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tenqs_5-3"><a href="#cite_note-tenqs-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="British_Championship_Wrestling_.282003.E2.80.932007.29">British Championship Wrestling (2003–2007)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Drew_Galloway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: British Championship Wrestling (2003–2007)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2003, Galloway made his debut for the inaugural show of British Championship Wrestling (BCW), operating in the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Glasgow" title="Greater Glasgow">Greater Glasgow</a> area. While there he honed his wrestling skill further, training under Colin McKay and later Spinner McKenzie<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tenqs_5-4"><a href="#cite_note-tenqs-5">[5]</a></sup> and developing the character of "Thee" Drew Galloway, a cocky <a href="/wiki/Narcissism" title="Narcissism">narcissist</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ramblings_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-ramblings-11">[11]</a></sup> His first match, which took place at February's <i>No Blood, No Sympathy: Night 1</i>, saw him lose against Stu Natt.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bcw1_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-bcw1-12">[12]</a></sup> He picked up his first win on the second night in a tag team match alongside Wolfgang, defeating Blade and Stu Pendous.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bcw2_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-bcw2-13">[13]</a></sup> By December, Galloway was <a href="/wiki/Manager_(professional_wrestling)" title="Manager (professional wrestling)">managed</a> by Charles Boddington, who aided him in his first significant success and would manage him for the next four years. On 5 December, Boddington announced that BCW Heavyweight Champion Spinner McKenzie had been fired and would be stripped of the title; Boddington then instantly gave the belt to Galloway.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bcwtitle_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-bcwtitle-14">[14]</a></sup> Stevie Knight took exception to this and challenged him to a match that very night at <i>Bad Tidings: Night 1</i>, winning the championship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bcw3_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-bcw3-15">[15]</a></sup> Galloway earned a non-title win over Knight the following February in 2004, at <i>Night of The Fan</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bcw4_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-bcw4-16">[16]</a></sup> but Knight exacted revenge by knocking Galloway out of the King of BCW tournament.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bcw5_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-bcw5-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>Later that year, Galloway had a series of matches against American veterans. In June, he was defeated by <a href="/wiki/The_Honky_Tonk_Man" title="The Honky Tonk Man">The Honky Tonk Man</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bcw6_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-bcw6-18">[18]</a></sup> and later that month lost in a tag team match to <a href="/wiki/Marty_Jannetty" title="Marty Jannetty">Marty Jannetty</a> and Highlander, with Sabotage on his side.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bcw7_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-bcw7-19">[19]</a></sup> In November at the aptly titled <i>Lo Down</i>, Galloway main evented in a double countout match against <a href="/wiki/D%27Lo_Brown" title="D'Lo Brown">D'Lo Brown</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bcw8_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-bcw8-20">[20]</a></sup> He then had a brief series of feuds, as in March 2005 he defeated Jay Phoenix<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bcw9_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-bcw9-21">[21]</a></sup> but their rematch in November, officiated by <a href="/wiki/Mick_Foley" title="Mick Foley">Mick Foley</a>, ended in a no contest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bcw10_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-bcw10-22">[22]</a></sup> In May 2006 after their lengthy feud in <a href="/wiki/Irish_Whip_Wrestling" title="Irish Whip Wrestling">Irish Whip Wrestling</a>, Galloway lost<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bcw11_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-bcw11-23">[23]</a></sup> then won in successive matches against long-term rival <a href="/wiki/Sheamus" title="Sheamus">Sheamus O'Shaunessy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bcw12_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-bcw12-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>In November 2006, in the main event of <i>Live in <a href="/wiki/East_Kilbride" title="East Kilbride">East Kilbride</a></i>, Galloway teamed with <a href="/wiki/Lionheart_(wrestler)" title="Lionheart (wrestler)">Lionheart</a> and pinned BCW Heavyweight Champion Highlander who was tagging with Wolfgang.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bcw13_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-bcw13-25">[25]</a></sup> This put him in contention for the title at December's No Blood, No Sympathy IV. The match was booked as an <a href="/wiki/%22I_Quit%22_match" title='"I Quit" match'>"I Quit" match</a> with Conscience as the special guest referee with Galloway gaining his second BCW Heavyweight Championship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bcwtitle_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-bcwtitle-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bcwtitlewin_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-bcwtitlewin-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bcw14_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-bcw14-27">[27]</a></sup> He held the title through most of 2007, with successful defenses over <a href="/wiki/Martin_Stone_(wrestler)" title="Martin Stone (wrestler)">Martin Stone</a>, Allan Grogan and <a href="/wiki/Lionheart_(wrestler)" title="Lionheart (wrestler)">Lionheart</a>, before vacating it<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bcwtitle_14-2"><a href="#cite_note-bcwtitle-14">[14]</a></sup> after he relocated to the United States in September.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slambio_2-3"><a href="#cite_note-slambio-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Irish_Whip_Wrestling_.282005.E2.80.932006.29">Irish Whip Wrestling (2005–2006)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Drew_Galloway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Irish Whip Wrestling (2005–2006)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After gaining momentum in Scotland, Galloway began wrestling dates across the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Republic of Ireland</a> with <a href="/wiki/Irish_Whip_Wrestling" title="Irish Whip Wrestling">Irish Whip Wrestling</a> (IwW) continuing to use "Thee" Drew Galloway as his gimmick. With Charles Boddington still in his corner, he competed in three contests during his first appearance on 23 July 2005 for <i>Whiplash TV</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ramblings_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-ramblings-11">[11]</a></sup> After losing to "SOS" <a href="/wiki/Sheamus" title="Sheamus">Sheamus O'Shaunessy</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iww1_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-iww1-28">[28]</a></sup> he found a similar fate against Mad Man Manson, sparking a feud between the two.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ramblings_11-2"><a href="#cite_note-ramblings-11">[11]</a></sup> Despite these two losses, his status abroad meant he was already booked in a <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling_match_types#Gauntlet_match" title="Professional wrestling match types">Ten-Man Gauntlet match</a> to determine the top contender for the main title. Galloway was whitewashed the entire evening, losing to Vic Viper.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iww1_28-1"><a href="#cite_note-iww1-28">[28]</a></sup> The following day at <i>Gym Wars</i> Manson was absent so Galloway tried to avenge his loss with O'Shaunessy but it ended in a double count-out.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iww2_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-iww2-29">[29]</a></sup> Over the next few months Galloway recruited various wrestlers, even his manager Boddington, in a series of <a href="/wiki/Tag_team" title="Tag team">tag team</a> and even <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_professional_wrestling_match_types#Handicap_match" title="List of professional wrestling match types">handicap tag team</a> matches against Manson and his teams.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iww3_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-iww3-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iww4_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-iww4-31">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iww5_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-iww5-32">[32]</a></sup> He picked up his first victory in October against Sean South in a warm-up for that event's main event six-man tag team match.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iww4_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-iww4-31">[31]</a></sup> The rivalry between Galloway and Manson was finally settled in November at IwW's final show from the SFX Theatre. Their brutal and bloody <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling_match_types#Hardcore-based_variations" title="Professional wrestling match types">Street Fight</a> saw Galloway gain respect from for his tenacity and endurance<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ramblings_11-3"><a href="#cite_note-ramblings-11">[11]</a></sup> but his losing streak continued.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iww7_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-iww7-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:IWW_Champion_Drew.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="450" data-file-width="600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/IWW_Champion_Drew.jpg/220px-IWW_Champion_Drew.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/IWW_Champion_Drew.jpg/330px-IWW_Champion_Drew.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/IWW_Champion_Drew.jpg/440px-IWW_Champion_Drew.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:IWW_Champion_Drew.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Galloway as the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Whip_Wrestling#Irish_Whip_Wrestling_International_Heavyweight_Championship" title="Irish Whip Wrestling">IWW International Heavyweight Champion</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>With his rivalry against Manson settled in their Street Fight and despite having only won one match with the company, Galloway was given a shot at the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Whip_Wrestling#Irish_Whip_Wrestling_International_Heavyweight_Championship" title="Irish Whip Wrestling">IwW International Heavyweight Championship</a> owing to his show stealing performances with Manson.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ramblings_11-4"><a href="#cite_note-ramblings-11">[11]</a></sup> On 28 January 2006 he received his first title match against Sheamus O'Shaunessy, evolving their rivalry from previous battles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iww8_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-iww8-34">[34]</a></sup> The rivalry quickly took on a patriotic flavour, with Galloway's blue colours of Scotland clashing O'Shaunessy's green colours of Ireland, mirroring the <a href="/wiki/Old_Firm" title="Old Firm">Old Firm</a> <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Local_derby" title="Local derby">derby</a> between <a href="/wiki/Rangers_F.C." title="Rangers F.C.">Glasgow Rangers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Celtic_F.C." title="Celtic F.C.">Glasgow Celtic</a>, respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ramblings_11-5"><a href="#cite_note-ramblings-11">[11]</a></sup> This football allusion became particularly prominent when the two met again at Verona Football Club once again for the title, though the match changed into a <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling_match_types#Lumberjack_match" title="Professional wrestling match types">Lumberjack match</a>, the result and champion remained the same.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iww9_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-iww9-35">[35]</a></sup> Galloway remained focussed, proving his dominance and determination for the championship by defeating JC Williams and Brian Roche in a handicap match on 17 March.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iww11_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-iww11-36">[36]</a></sup> This match earned him a <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling_match_types#Series_variations" title="Professional wrestling match types">two out of three falls match</a> against the champion the following day in which O'Shaunessy won two falls to one;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iww12_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-iww12-37">[37]</a></sup> the next day produced the same result.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iww13_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-iww13-38">[38]</a></sup> Again Galloway proved himself a fierce competitor, twice making Vic Viper acquiesce in <a href="/wiki/%22I_Quit%22_match" title='"I Quit" match'>"I Quit" matches</a> in April.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iww14_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-iww14-39">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iww15_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-iww15-40">[40]</a></sup> With their rivalry intensifying, Galloway's next challenge to O'Shaunessy was given the stipulation of a <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling_match_types#Last_Man_Standing_match" title="Professional wrestling match types">Last Man Standing match</a>. Once again, the Irish native retained the title,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iww16_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-iww16-41">[41]</a></sup> as he also did in June with the same stipulation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iww17_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-iww17-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p>Finally, on 28 August 2006 Galloway managed to beat the reigning Irishman and won the IwW International Heavyweight Championship in a singles match.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iwwtitle_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-iwwtitle-44">[44]</a></sup> He successfully defended the belt that evening against <a href="/wiki/Go_Shiozaki" title="Go Shiozaki">Go Shiozaki</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ramblings_11-6"><a href="#cite_note-ramblings-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iww17_42-1"><a href="#cite_note-iww17-42">[42]</a></sup> In November, Galloway took the championship to <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, England to defend it at <a href="/wiki/Real_Quality_Wrestling" title="Real Quality Wrestling">Real Quality Wrestling</a>'s <i>Rebirth</i> in November against <a href="/wiki/Jody_Fleisch" title="Jody Fleisch">Jody Fleisch</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rebirth_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-rebirth-45">[45]</a></sup> though the match was broadcast on 20 December episode of RQW TV.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rqwtv_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-rqwtv-46">[46]</a></sup> However, Galloway was not able to commit to fully defending the title, due to other bookings in his homeland and his academic studies, he was thus forced to relinquish the championship in January 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ramblings_11-7"><a href="#cite_note-ramblings-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iwwstrip_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-iwwstrip-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Touring_Great_Britain_.282005.E2.80.932007.29">Touring Great Britain (2005–2007)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Drew_Galloway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Touring Great Britain (2005–2007)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>While BCW became his home promotion and he made regular appearances for IwW, Galloway made several appearances around the independent circuit. In 2004, he appeared for the fledgling <a href="/wiki/International_Pro_Wrestling:_United_Kingdom" title="International Pro Wrestling: United Kingdom">International Pro Wrestling: United Kingdom</a> (IPW:UK) at their aptly titled <i>Show 2</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ipwdvd_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-ipwdvd-48">[48]</a></sup> Despite losing to <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Aviv_Maayan&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Aviv Maayan (page does not exist)">Aviv Maayan</a> in his first showing,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ipw1_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-ipw1-49">[49]</a></sup> by the time he returned in May 2005 his reputation made him notorious enough to compete in their main event Five Way Elimination match to determine the best of British heavyweights. Galloway was eliminated first by <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Simmons" title="Andrew Simmons">Andy Boy Simmonz</a> with a <a href="/wiki/Pin_(professional_wrestling)#Small_package" title="Pin (professional wrestling)">small package</a> pin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ipw2_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-ipw2-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<p>In between studying, Gallow competed in several tours of <a href="/wiki/All_Star_Wrestling" title="All Star Wrestling">All Star Wrestling</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slambio_2-4"><a href="#cite_note-slambio-2">[2]</a></sup> against competitors including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/TJ_Wilson" title="TJ Wilson">TJ Wilson</a>, PN Neuz, <a href="/wiki/Chad_Collyer" title="Chad Collyer">Chad Collyer</a> and Brody Steele during 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-btw_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-btw-51">[51]</a></sup> On 15 October 2006, Galloway competed in Insane Championship Wrestling's (ICW) debut show <i>Fear &amp; Loathing</i>, defeating Darkside and Allan Grogan in a <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling_match_types#Basic_non-elimination_matches" title="Professional wrestling match types">three-way</a> 30-minute <a href="/wiki/Iron_Man_match" title="Iron Man match">Iron Man match</a> to become the first ICW Heavyweight Champion. He held the title for 280 days, ultimately losing it to Darkside on 22 July 2007 in a five-man elimination match that also involved <a href="/wiki/Jack_Jester" title="Jack Jester">Jack Jester</a>, Wolfgang and Liam Thomson.</p>
<p>Despite it being his only match (he was used twice) for <a href="/wiki/National_Wrestling_Alliance" title="National Wrestling Alliance">NWA: Scottish Wrestling Alliance</a> (NWA:SWA), Galloway represented Team SWA against Team Sinner in the titular match for the March 2006 <i>Clan Wars</i> event, being eliminated first by Highlander who was using the ropes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-swa_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-swa-52">[52]</a></sup> At the end of the month he appeared at the inaugural event for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Premier_British_Wrestling" title="Premier British Wrestling">Premier British Wrestling</a> (PBW) earning a shot to become the first PBW Heavyweight Champion by defeating Allan Grogan but losing to Wolfgang in the main event. In October he was entered into a contendership match to win another chance at the title, but was beaten by Dave Moralez.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pbw6_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-pbw6-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>Galloway's reputation continued to precede him, being placed in contention for <a href="/wiki/Real_Quality_Wrestling" title="Real Quality Wrestling">RQW's</a> <i>Not Just For Christmas</i> tournament to crown the inaugural <a href="/wiki/RQW_Heavyweight_Championship" title="RQW Heavyweight Championship">RQW Heavyweight Champion</a>. Representing IwW, having made his IwW Title defence against Fleisch earlier in the year, Galloway faced SAS Wrestling's <a href="/wiki/El_Ligero" title="El Ligero">El Ligero</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-xmas_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-xmas-54">[54]</a></sup> going through to the semi-final only to lose to <a href="/wiki/One_Pro_Wrestling" title="One Pro Wrestling">One Pro Wrestling</a>'s Pac by count out. Galloway continued to appear in April, taking his rivalry with 'SOS' Sheamus O'Shaunessy to London with a double count-out<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rqwapr_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-rqwapr-55">[55]</a></sup> which led to a rematch in June where Galloway picked up the victory in a Street Fight. Later on that evening, having made a statement with his win over O'Shaunessy, Galloway attacked the RQW Heavyweight Champion <a href="/wiki/Martin_Stone_(wrestler)" title="Martin Stone (wrestler)">Martin Stone</a> during his title defence against <a href="/wiki/Takeshi_Rikio" title="Takeshi Rikio">Takeshi Rikio</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rqwjune_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-rqwjune-56">[56]</a></sup> This attack led to Galloway's final match in the UK at August's <i>Summer Brawl</i>. Despite attacking Stone earlier in the evening, Galloway could not pick up the victory and failed to win the title.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rqwbrawl_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-rqwbrawl-57">[57]</a></sup> Galloway's very last appearance was serving as a referee for PBW on 15 September in a match that saw Darkside defeat Lionheart to become the championship contender.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Insane_Championship_Wrestling_.282006.E2.80.932007.29">Insane Championship Wrestling (2006–2007)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Drew_Galloway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Insane Championship Wrestling (2006–2007)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Galloway appeared on the inaugural <a href="/wiki/Insane_Championship_Wrestling" title="Insane Championship Wrestling">Insane Championship Wrestling</a> show promoted by a young <a href="/wiki/Mark_Dallas" title="Mark Dallas">Mark Dallas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> Galloway won a triple threat match over Darkside and Allan Grogan to become the first ever <a href="/wiki/ICW_World_Heavyweight_Championship_(Scotland)" title="ICW World Heavyweight Championship (Scotland)">ICW Heavyweight Champion</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> Galloway held the title for 280 days, retaining over <a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_(wrestler)" title="Wolfgang (wrestler)">Wolfgang</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> and Allan Grogan,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> before losing the title to Darkside in a five-man match which also included <a href="/wiki/Jack_Jester" title="Jack Jester">Jack Jester</a>, Wolfgang and Liam Thomson.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> This was his final appearance for the company until 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_Wrestling_Entertainment.2FWWE">World Wrestling Entertainment/WWE</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Drew_Galloway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: World Wrestling Entertainment/WWE">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_appearances_and_Ohio_Valley_Wrestling_.282006.E2.80.932007.29">Early appearances and Ohio Valley Wrestling (2006–2007)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Drew_Galloway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Early appearances and Ohio Valley Wrestling (2006–2007)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In late 2006, <a href="/wiki/WWE" title="WWE">World Wrestling Entertainment</a> (WWE) went on tour in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> and before their filming of <i><a href="/wiki/WWE_SmackDown" title="WWE SmackDown">SmackDown!</a></i> in Manchester, Galloway had a try out match against O'Shaunessy. The following year in April, the two received another try out match in London.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fights_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-fights-68">[68]</a></sup> Later on 12 October 2007, Galloway made his televised WWE debut during <i>SmackDown!</i> using the name Drew McIntyre. He appeared as a fan friendly character, imploring the crowd to cheer for him due to seeking <a href="/wiki/Multiple_citizenship" title="Multiple citizenship">dual citizenship</a> with America while accompanied by fellow Briton <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dave_Taylor_(wrestler,_born_1957)" title="Dave Taylor (wrestler, born 1957)">Dave Taylor</a>. He defeated <a href="/wiki/Zack_Ryder" title="Zack Ryder">Brett Major</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sd1210_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-sd1210-69">[69]</a></sup> and on the following episode of <i>SmackDown!</i>, McIntyre defeated Brett's tag team partner <a href="/wiki/Curt_Hawkins" title="Curt Hawkins">Brian Major</a> with the help of Taylor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> McIntyre was moved to the <a href="/wiki/WWE_Raw" title="WWE Raw">Raw</a> <a href="/wiki/WWE_brand_extension" title="WWE brand extension">brand</a> in the new year, but after a win against <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Haas" title="Charlie Haas">Charlie Haas</a> on 4 January he disappeared from television.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-heat_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-heat-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<p>After moving to <a href="/wiki/Kentucky" title="Kentucky">Kentucky</a>, Galloway made his debut in <a href="/wiki/Ohio_Valley_Wrestling" title="Ohio Valley Wrestling">Ohio Valley Wrestling</a> (OVW) on 26 September with a win over fellow FWA Academy alumnus <a href="/wiki/Paul_Burchill" title="Paul Burchill">Paul Burchill</a>. He soon changed his name to Drew McIntyre and teamed with Burchill to take on <a href="/wiki/Curt_Hawkins_and_Zack_Ryder" title="Curt Hawkins and Zack Ryder">The Major Brothers</a> (Brian and Brett) in a losing effort. In October, McIntyre found a new partner in <a href="/wiki/Wade_Barrett" title="Wade Barrett">Stu Sanders</a> forming a tag team called The Brit Pack. Still they failed to defeat The Major Brothers, both in a tag team match and a Four Corners tag team match elimination match. The Brit Pack picked up their first victory on 31 October TV tapings over Dirty Money and Scott Cardinal. The win propelled McIntyre to gain an <a href="/wiki/OVW_Television_Championship" title="OVW Television Championship">OVW Television Championship</a> match against <a href="/wiki/Colt_Cabana" title="Colt Cabana">Colt Cabana</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ovw07_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-ovw07-72">[72]</a></sup> In 2008, Mcintyre gained momentum with a winning streak that built towards a non-title match against <a href="/wiki/OVW_Heavyweight_Championship" title="OVW Heavyweight Championship">OVW Heavyweight Champion</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Evan_Bourne" title="Evan Bourne">Evan Bourne</a> which McIntyre won by disqualification. His final match in OVW was on 29 February with a win over Scott Cardinal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ovw08_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-ovw08-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Florida_Championship_Wrestling_.282007.E2.80.932009.29">Florida Championship Wrestling (2007–2009)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Drew_Galloway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Florida Championship Wrestling (2007–2009)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>After moving to <a href="/wiki/Florida_Championship_Wrestling" title="Florida Championship Wrestling">Florida Championship Wrestling</a> (FCW), Galloway reformed his team with Stu Sanders, now going under the name of The Empire. In April, they took on The Puerto Rican Nightmares (<a href="/wiki/Eric_P%C3%A9rez" title="Eric Pérez">Eric Pérez</a> and <a href="/wiki/Primo_(wrestler)" title="Primo (wrestler)">Eddie Colón</a>) who won the match and a title shot at the <a href="/wiki/FCW_Florida_Tag_Team_Championship" title="FCW Florida Tag Team Championship">FCW Florida Tag Team Championship</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fcw08_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-fcw08-74">[74]</a></sup> Once The Nightmares won the championship, The Empire received two consecutive chances to win the FCW Florida Tag Team Championship on 6 May.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FCWchampionships_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-FCWchampionships-75">[75]</a></sup> Their first title defence was against McIntyre's old rival Sheamus O'Shaunessy, but his partner <a href="/wiki/Steven_Lewington" title="Steven Lewington">"Sterling Jack" Gabriel</a> accidentally hit them and The Empire capitalised to retain their championship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fcw08_74-1"><a href="#cite_note-fcw08-74">[74]</a></sup> The Empire lost the championship on 17 July to <a href="/wiki/Curtis_Axel" title="Curtis Axel">Joe Hennig</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tyler_Reks" title="Tyler Reks">Gabe Tuft</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FCWchampionships_75-1"><a href="#cite_note-FCWchampionships-75">[75]</a></sup> On 16 August, The Empire imploded when McIntyre faced Sanders in a singles match which ended in a double countout and their rematch at the end of September ended in a time limit draw.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Drew_McIntyre_Hoisting_up_FCW_Championship.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Drew_McIntyre_Hoisting_up_FCW_Championship.jpg/220px-Drew_McIntyre_Hoisting_up_FCW_Championship.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Drew_McIntyre_Hoisting_up_FCW_Championship.jpg/330px-Drew_McIntyre_Hoisting_up_FCW_Championship.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Drew_McIntyre_Hoisting_up_FCW_Championship.jpg/440px-Drew_McIntyre_Hoisting_up_FCW_Championship.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Drew_McIntyre_Hoisting_up_FCW_Championship.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Galloway with the Florida Heavyweight Championship belt</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 7 October, McIntyre was entered into a contest for the <a href="/wiki/FCW_Florida_Heavyweight_Championship" title="FCW Florida Heavyweight Championship">FCW Florida Heavyweight Championship</a> and defeated Tuft to make it into the final but lost to Eric Escobar (the former Eric Peréz). McIntyre closed out the year with an unsuccessful attempt to gain the FCW Florida Heavyweight Championship in a four-way match, but Escobar won the title from O'Shaunessy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fcwh_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-fcwh-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<p>Going into 2009, McIntyre entered into a rivalry with Joe Hennig, but their first match in February ended in a double countout. McIntyre interfered in Hennig's match the following week, costing him the match. On 26 February, Hennig defeated McIntyre<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fcw09_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-fcw09-77">[77]</a></sup> and went on that night to win the FCW Florida Heavyweight Championship from Escobar. Their feud ended abruptly when Hennig vacated the title after an injury, causing McIntyre to be elevated into title contendership, beating Escobar for the vacant championship on 19 March. McIntyre regularly defended the title until 11 June, when Tyler Reks (the former Gabe Tuft) won the title in his second attempt.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fcwh_76-1"><a href="#cite_note-fcwh-76">[76]</a></sup> Later that month, McIntyre failed to win a 14-man battle royal for a chance to regain the title. On 25 June, McIntyre was set to team with O'Shaunessy against the returning Hennig and DJ Gabriel (the aforementioned "Sterling Jack" Gabriel), but when neither team would work together a four-way was booked, which O'Shaunessy won. McIntyre and O'Shaunessy both failed to win back the FCW Florida Heavyweight Championship in mid-July from Reks. McIntyre received a singles opportunity the next day with the same result.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fcw09_77-1"><a href="#cite_note-fcw09-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Chosen_One_.282009.E2.80.932011.29">The Chosen One (2009–2011)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Drew_Galloway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: The Chosen One (2009–2011)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Drew_mcintyre.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Drew_mcintyre.jpg/220px-Drew_mcintyre.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Drew_mcintyre.jpg/330px-Drew_mcintyre.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Drew_mcintyre.jpg/440px-Drew_mcintyre.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Drew_mcintyre.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
McIntyre in a match against <a href="/wiki/Dave_Finlay" title="Dave Finlay">Finlay</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 28 August 2009, McIntyre re-debuted on the SmackDown brand, disregarding his previous time on WWE television, and established himself as a villain by attacking <a href="/wiki/Ron_Killings" title="Ron Killings">R-Truth</a> as he entered the ring, using his new <a href="/wiki/DDT_(professional_wrestling)#Double_underhook_DDT" title="DDT (professional wrestling)">double underhook DDT</a> finishing move, the <i>Scot Drop</i> (soon renamed the <i>Future Shock</i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sd2808_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-sd2808-78">[78]</a></sup> McIntyre continued to attack Truth over the following weeks, claiming to be on the show to wrestle not to party like R-Truth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> On 18 September, while Charlie Haas was waiting to face R-Truth, McIntyre came to the ring to explain that R-Truth had been injured backstage, and then attacked Haas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sd189_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-sd189-80">[80]</a></sup> On 25 September, WWE Chairman <a href="/wiki/Vince_McMahon#Professional_wrestling" title="Vince McMahon">Mr. McMahon</a> introduced McIntyre as a "future world champion" that he had personally signed, after which Truth made a return attack against McIntyre.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sd269_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-sd269-81">[81]</a></sup> The following week on <i>SmackDown</i>, McIntyre continued to crash parties by making a speech at the <i><a href="/wiki/WWE_SmackDown#Special_episodes" title="WWE SmackDown">Decade of SmackDown</a></i> celebration until R-Truth put him through a table and the anniversary cake.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sd210_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-sd210-82">[82]</a></sup> This all led to McIntyre's first proper match since his return at the <a href="/wiki/Hell_in_a_Cell_(2009)" title="Hell in a Cell (2009)">Hell in a Cell</a> pay-per-view (PPV), where McIntyre defeated R-Truth in under five minutes again using his DDT finisher.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HIAC_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-HIAC-83">[83]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hiactime_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-hiactime-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<p>McIntyre faced R-Truth once more in a singles match and won by countout to represent SmackDown at <a href="/wiki/Bragging_Rights_(2009)" title="Bragging Rights (2009)">Bragging Rights</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> but the episode before the PPV the entire team, captains aside, was replaced leaving McIntyre omitted from the event.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> McIntyre briefly feuded with <a href="/wiki/Dave_Finlay" title="Dave Finlay">Finlay</a> in the same manner as Truth with matches not starting properly<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sd3110_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-sd3110-88">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sd1311_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-sd1311-89">[89]</a></sup> until McIntyre won their final meeting in under two minutes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sd2011_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-sd2011-90">[90]</a></sup> At <a href="/wiki/Survivor_Series_(2009)" title="Survivor Series (2009)">Survivor Series</a> on 24 November, McIntyre had a place on <a href="/wiki/The_Miz" title="The Miz">The Miz</a>'s team for the traditional <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling_tag_team_match_types#Elimination_tag_team_matches" title="Professional wrestling tag team match types">Survivor Series elimination match</a>. McIntyre, The Miz and his former rival Sheamus (previously Sheamus O'Shaunessy) were the surviving members on their winning team; McIntyre eliminated <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Evan_Bourne" title="Evan Bourne">Evan Bourne</a> and <a href="/wiki/Matt_Hardy" title="Matt Hardy">Matt Hardy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ss09_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-ss09-91">[91]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:IC_Champion_Drew_McIntyre.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/IC_Champion_Drew_McIntyre.jpg/220px-IC_Champion_Drew_McIntyre.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/IC_Champion_Drew_McIntyre.jpg/330px-IC_Champion_Drew_McIntyre.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/IC_Champion_Drew_McIntyre.jpg/440px-IC_Champion_Drew_McIntyre.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:IC_Champion_Drew_McIntyre.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
McIntyre as the <a href="/wiki/WWE_Intercontinental_Championship" title="WWE Intercontinental Championship">Intercontinental Champion</a> in December 2009</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Being the only SmackDown superstar to survive against Team Morrison, McIntyre faced and defeated <a href="/wiki/John_Morrison_(wrestler)" title="John Morrison (wrestler)">John Morrison</a> a few weeks later,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sd412_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-sd412-92">[92]</a></sup> putting him in line for Morrison's <a href="/wiki/WWE_Intercontinental_Championship" title="WWE Intercontinental Championship">Intercontinental Championship</a> at <a href="/wiki/TLC:_Tables,_Ladders_%26_Chairs_(2009)" title="TLC: Tables, Ladders &amp; Chairs (2009)">TLC: Tables, Ladders &amp; Chairs</a> (TLC). Days before the event, Morrison mocked McIntyre's Scottish heritage by dressing as a <i><a href="/wiki/Braveheart" title="Braveheart">Braveheart</a></i>-inspired <a href="/wiki/William_Wallace" title="William Wallace">William Wallace</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sd1112_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-sd1112-93">[93]</a></sup> but at TLC on 13 December, McIntyre managed to pin Morrison after a thumb to the eye to win the Intercontinental title, his first championship in WWE.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tlc_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-tlc-94">[94]</a></sup> He retained the title against Morrison and later against <a href="/wiki/Kane_(wrestler)" title="Kane (wrestler)">Kane</a> using underhanded tactics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sd101_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-sd101-95">[95]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ec10_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-ec10-96">[96]</a></sup> His televised undefeated record ended in a <a href="/wiki/Money_in_the_Bank_ladder_match" title="Money in the Bank ladder match">Money in the Bank</a> qualifying match against Kane on 26 February episode of <i>SmackDown</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sd2602_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-sd2602-97">[97]</a></sup> but Mr McMahon forced SmackDown's general manager <a href="/wiki/Theodore_Long" title="Theodore Long">Teddy Long</a> to expunge the loss. The same thing happened again with <a href="/wiki/Matt_Hardy" title="Matt Hardy">Matt Hardy</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sd53_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-sd53-98">[98]</a></sup> before McIntyre finally qualified for the Ladder match by pinning an unsigned wrestler.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sd123_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-sd123-99">[99]</a></sup> He then lost to <a href="/wiki/The_Undertaker" title="The Undertaker">The Undertaker</a> on 19 March<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sd193_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-sd193-100">[100]</a></sup> and he also failed to win the Money in the Bank match on 29 March at <a href="/wiki/WrestleMania_XXVI" title="WrestleMania XXVI">WrestleMania XXVI</a>, his first WrestleMania appearance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wm26_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-wm26-101">[101]</a></sup> In weeks after this, McIntyre continuously attacked Matt Hardy until he was stripped of his title on 7 May by Long and suspended for the purposes of the storyline;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sd75_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-sd75-102">[102]</a></sup> McMahon decreed he be reinstated as champion the following week, undermining Long's authority which developed tension between McIntyre and Long.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sd145_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-sd145-103">[103]</a></sup> As a result, McIntyre faced <a href="/wiki/Kofi_Kingston" title="Kofi Kingston">Kofi Kingston</a> – who had won a tournament to determine the new champion – at <a href="/wiki/Over_the_Limit_(2010)" title="Over the Limit (2010)">Over the Limit</a> on 23 May, and lost the championship after 161 days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> McIntyre, however, still used his relationship with McMahon to bully Teddy Long, publicly humiliating and forcing Long to lie down for him for their match.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> At <a href="/wiki/WWE_Fatal_4-Way" title="WWE Fatal 4-Way">Fatal 4-Way</a> on 20 June, McIntyre faced Kingston in a rematch for the Intercontinental Championship. During the match, Long took over as the referee, but he refused to make the three count when McIntyre had the match won. A vengeful Matt Hardy then attacked McIntyre, leading to Kingston winning the match and retaining the championship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 21 June episode of <i>Raw</i>, <a href="/wiki/The_Nexus_(professional_wrestling)" title="The Nexus (professional wrestling)">The Nexus</a> faction attacked McMahon which removed him from television for a prolonged period and ended McIntyre's preferential treatment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> After losing to Matt Hardy on 25 June episode of <i>SmackDown</i>, Long informed McIntyre that his work visa had expired and that he would be deported back to Scotland immediately.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> This storyline had a basis in reality, since Galloway's visa had indeed expired and as a result he was taken off television.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> He returned two weeks later and was re-instated after being made to beg Long and qualified for the eponymous match at the <a href="/wiki/Money_in_the_Bank_(2010)" title="Money in the Bank (2010)">Money in the Bank</a> PPV by defeating Kofi Kingston.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> McIntyre then continued his rivalry with Matt Hardy and Hardy's friend <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Christian_(wrestler)" title="Christian (wrestler)">Christian</a>. At the same time, "Dashing" <a href="/wiki/Cody_Rhodes" title="Cody Rhodes">Cody Rhodes</a> also took umbrage with Matt Hardy and Christian, leading to an alliance being formed. On 19 September at <a href="/wiki/Night_of_Champions_(2010)" title="Night of Champions (2010)">Night of Champions</a>, McIntyre and Rhodes captured the <a href="/wiki/WWE_Raw_Tag_Team_Championship" title="WWE Raw Tag Team Championship">WWE Tag Team Championship</a> in a five-team <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling_tag_team_match_types#Tag_team_turmoil" title="Professional wrestling tag team match types">tag team turmoil match</a> as the last entrants. This allowed them to appear on both brands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NightofChampions2010_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-NightofChampions2010-111">[111]</a></sup> McIntyre and Rhodes then successfully defended their championship twice against <a href="/wiki/The_Hart_Dynasty" title="The Hart Dynasty">The Hart Dynasty</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/Bragging_Rights_(2010)" title="Bragging Rights (2010)">Bragging Rights</a> PPV on 24 October, McIntyre and Rhodes lost the championship to The Nexus (<a href="/wiki/John_Cena" title="John Cena">John Cena</a> and <a href="/wiki/David_Otunga" title="David Otunga">David Otunga</a>) and dissolved their team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> On 21 November at <a href="/wiki/Survivor_Series_(2010)" title="Survivor Series (2010)">Survivor Series</a>, McIntyre participated in a 5-on-5 traditional Survivor Series tag team match as a member of Team Del Rio against Team Mysterio. McIntyre would be the final man remaining on his team before he was eliminated by <a href="/wiki/Big_Show" title="Big Show">Big Show</a>. McIntyre would participate in the 40 man Royal Rumble match on 30 January, but would be eliminated by Big Show.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Various_storylines_and_brand_switches_.282011.E2.80.932012.29">Various storylines and brand switches (2011–2012)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Drew_Galloway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Various storylines and brand switches (2011–2012)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In early 2011, McIntyre was part of a brief storyline with <a href="/wiki/Kelly_Kelly" title="Kelly Kelly">Kelly Kelly</a>. Though Kelly was a popular character, McIntyre tried to woo her despite his villainous behavior. She refused to date him, due to his anger problems which were shown during his matches against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trent_Barretta" title="Trent Barretta">Trent Barretta</a>. In February, He participated in the SmackDown Elimination Chamber match for the World Heavyweight Championship but was eliminated by Kane. After being continually spurned by Kelly, McIntyre teamed with <a href="/wiki/Vickie_Guerrero" title="Vickie Guerrero">Vickie Guerrero</a> in a losing effort against Kelly and <a href="/wiki/Edge_(wrestler)" title="Edge (wrestler)">Edge</a> on 22 February episode of <i>SmackDown</i>.</p>
<p>On 26 April, Drew McIntyre was drafted to the Raw brand as part of the <a href="/wiki/2011_WWE_draft#Supplemental_draft" title="2011 WWE draft">2011 supplemental draft</a> and made his debut for the brand in a losing effort to Kofi Kingston.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> McIntyre featured very rarely on <i>Raw</i> and was confined to dark matches and <i><a href="/wiki/WWE_Superstars" title="WWE Superstars">Superstars</a></i>.</p>
<p>On 15 December episode of <i>Superstars</i>, McIntyre finally won a match by defeating <a href="/wiki/Justin_Gabriel" title="Justin Gabriel">Justin Gabriel</a> which earned him a contract with <i>SmackDown</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> He switched to the SmackDown brand on 30 December and resumed his tense relationship with General Manager <a href="/wiki/Theodore_Long" title="Theodore Long">Theodore Long</a>. Long put pressure on McIntyre to win matches to justify his contract and McIntyre subsequently began an eight match losing streak going into the new year,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> after the last of which, Long fired McIntyre within the storyline.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> A week later, McIntyre was reinstated by guest general manager <a href="/wiki/John_Laurinaitis" title="John Laurinaitis">John Laurinaitis</a>, where he finally ended his losing streak by defeating <a href="/wiki/Hornswoggle" title="Hornswoggle">Hornswoggle</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> He was subsequently included on Laurinaitis' team in the 12-man Tag Team match at <a href="/wiki/WrestleMania_XXVIII" title="WrestleMania XXVIII">WrestleMania XXVIII</a>, helping to earn Laurinaitis control of both the Raw and SmackDown brands. During the match, Drew McIntyre injured his shoulder. He returned on the 10 May episode of <i>Superstars</i> defeating <a href="/wiki/Ezekiel_Jackson" title="Ezekiel Jackson">Ezekiel Jackson</a>. Since returning his fortunes had relatively stayed the same. He continued to lose most matches and was confined to Superstars and house shows. However, he was able to make several appearances on <i>Raw</i> and <i>SmackDown</i>, but most of them were squash matches against the likes of <a href="/wiki/Brodus_Clay" title="Brodus Clay">Brodus Clay</a>.</p>
<p>When WWE <a href="/wiki/Rebranding" title="Rebranding">rebranded</a> its developmental territory, FCW, into NXT Wrestling,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FCWtoNXT_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-FCWtoNXT-120">[120]</a></sup> McIntyre was inserted into the Gold Rush Tournament to crown the inaugural <a href="/wiki/NXT_Championship" title="NXT Championship">NXT Champion</a>, where he lost to <a href="/wiki/Seth_Rollins" title="Seth Rollins">Seth Rollins</a> in the quarter-finals on 1 August episode of <i>NXT</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> McIntyre also participated in a number one contender fatal four-way elimination match on 7 November episode of <i>NXT</i>, but was eliminated by <a href="/wiki/Bo_Dallas" title="Bo Dallas">Bo Dallas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="3MB_.282012.E2.80.932014.29">3MB (2012–2014)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Drew_Galloway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: 3MB (2012–2014)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Drew_McIntyre_April_2014.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3986" data-file-width="2848" height="308" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Drew_McIntyre_April_2014.jpg/220px-Drew_McIntyre_April_2014.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Drew_McIntyre_April_2014.jpg/330px-Drew_McIntyre_April_2014.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Drew_McIntyre_April_2014.jpg/440px-Drew_McIntyre_April_2014.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Drew_McIntyre_April_2014.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
McIntyre as a member of 3MB</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:3MB_at_WM30.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2613" data-file-width="3154" height="182" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/3MB_at_WM30.jpg/220px-3MB_at_WM30.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/3MB_at_WM30.jpg/330px-3MB_at_WM30.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/3MB_at_WM30.jpg/440px-3MB_at_WM30.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:3MB_at_WM30.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
3MB in 2014</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 21 September episode of <i>SmackDown</i>, McIntyre and <a href="/wiki/Jinder_Mahal" title="Jinder Mahal">Jinder Mahal</a> interfered in a match between <a href="/wiki/Heath_Slater" title="Heath Slater">Heath Slater</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brodus_Clay" title="Brodus Clay">Brodus Clay</a> by attacking Clay, aligning themselves with Slater.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> The trio became known as the Three Man Band, later shortened to 3MB.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> Due to a wrist injury, McIntyre managed Slater and Mahal in tag matches.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> McIntyre returned to the ring from injury on 7 December episode of <i>SmackDown</i> when 3MB defeated the team of <a href="/wiki/The_Usos" title="The Usos">The Usos</a> and Brodus Clay.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> At <a href="/wiki/TLC:_Tables,_Ladders_%26_Chairs_(2012)" title="TLC: Tables, Ladders &amp; Chairs (2012)">TLC: Tables, Ladders &amp; Chairs</a>, after being guests on <i>Miz TV</i> and harassing the Spanish announce team, 3MB challenged <a href="/wiki/The_Miz" title="The Miz">The Miz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alberto_Del_Rio" title="Alberto Del Rio">Alberto Del Rio</a> to find a partner for a six-man tag team match for later that night. Miz would announce their partner to be the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Brawler" title="Brooklyn Brawler">Brooklyn Brawler</a>, and would go on to defeat 3MB.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> The next night on <i>Raw</i>, 3MB were defeated by The Miz and Del Rio again, this time with <a href="/wiki/Tommy_Dreamer" title="Tommy Dreamer">Tommy Dreamer</a> as their partner.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> On 31 December episode of <i>Raw</i>, McIntyre and Slater challenged <a href="/wiki/Team_Hell_No" title="Team Hell No">Team Hell No</a> (<a href="/wiki/Daniel_Bryan" title="Daniel Bryan">Daniel Bryan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kane_(wrestler)" title="Kane (wrestler)">Kane</a>) for the <a href="/wiki/WWE_Raw_Tag_Team_Championship" title="WWE Raw Tag Team Championship">WWE Tag Team Championship</a> in a losing effort.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> McIntyre and Slater also competed in the first round of the <a href="/wiki/NXT_Tag_Team_Championship" title="NXT Tag Team Championship">NXT Tag Team Championship</a> tournament to crown the inaugural champions, but were defeated by <a href="/wiki/Adrian_Neville" title="Adrian Neville">Adrian Neville</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oliver_Grey" title="Oliver Grey">Oliver Grey</a> on 23 January episode of <i>NXT</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 12 April episode of <i>SmackDown</i>, in an attempt to make a name for themselves, 3MB tried to attack <a href="/wiki/Triple_H" title="Triple H">Triple H</a>, but were attacked themselves by <a href="/wiki/The_Shield_(professional_wrestling)" title="The Shield (professional wrestling)">The Shield</a> (<a href="/wiki/Dean_Ambrose" title="Dean Ambrose">Dean Ambrose</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seth_Rollins" title="Seth Rollins">Seth Rollins</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roman_Reigns" title="Roman Reigns">Roman Reigns</a>). On 15 April episode of <i>Raw</i>, 3MB called out The Shield, only for <a href="/wiki/Brock_Lesnar" title="Brock Lesnar">Brock Lesnar</a> to come out instead and attack the group.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> On 29 April episode of <i>Raw</i>, 3MB attacked The Shield, but The Shield would quickly turn the tables on them. This resulted in Team Hell No chasing away The Shield, before attacking 3MB themselves.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> Beginning in late 2013, 3MB began adopting new ring names against their opponents, although their misfortunes and amounting losses remained the same. At <a href="/wiki/WrestleMania_XXX" title="WrestleMania XXX">WrestleMania XXX</a>, McIntyre competed in the André the Giant Memorial Battle Royal but was eliminated by Mark Henry. 3MB then formed an alliance with Hornswoggle to feud with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Los_Matadores" title="Los Matadores">Los Matadores</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mascarita_Dorada" title="Mascarita Dorada">El Torito</a>. On 12 June 2014, WWE announced that McIntyre was released from his WWE contract alongside Jinder Mahal, thus disbanding 3MB.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Return_to_ICW_.282014.E2.80.93present.29">Return to ICW (2014–present)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Drew_Galloway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Return to ICW (2014–present)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Having reverted to using his real name, Galloway made his first post-WWE appearance on 27 July 2014, returning to work for <a href="/wiki/Mark_Dallas" title="Mark Dallas">Mark Dallas</a> at <a href="/wiki/Insane_Championship_Wrestling" title="Insane Championship Wrestling">Insane Championship Wrestling</a> (ICW) for the first time in seven years and beginning a feud with <a href="/wiki/Jack_Jester" title="Jack Jester">Jack Jester</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> On 2 November at ICW's "Fear &amp; Loathing VII" event at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Barrowlands" title="The Barrowlands">The Barrowlands</a>, Galloway defeated Jester in the main event to become a two-time <a href="/wiki/ICW_World_Heavyweight_Championship_(Scotland)" title="ICW World Heavyweight Championship (Scotland)">ICW Heavyweight Champion</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> Galloway made his first defense in Glasgow on 7 December, defeating Kid Fite in the main event of ICW's "Brush Your Goose".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> Galloway made his first international ICW title defense in Denmark on 20 December in a double championship triple threat match against Danish Pro Wrestling Champion Michael Fynne and Chaos, where he both retained the ICW title and gained the DPW Heavyweight Championship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> Galloway competed in his final match of 2014 in a surprise appearance at ICW's "Space Baws 5: Bill Murray Strikes Back" by answering the challenge of Lewis Girvan, who had been goading Galloway for a match– Galloway defeated Girvan to retain the ICW Heavyweight Championship. Following the match, he announced his intention to make the title a <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling_championship#World_championships" title="Professional wrestling championship">world championship</a> by continuing to defend it internationally.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 25 January 2015 at the "Square Go" event, Galloway defeated rival Chris Renfrew to retain the belt. On 9 February, Galloway successfully defended his title against <a href="/wiki/Matt_Hardy" title="Matt Hardy">Matt Hardy</a> in a match for the <a href="/wiki/Family_Wrestling_Entertainment" title="Family Wrestling Entertainment">Family Wrestling Entertainment</a> promotion in New York, subsequently renaming it the <a href="/wiki/ICW_World_Heavyweight_Championship_(Scotland)" title="ICW World Heavyweight Championship (Scotland)">ICW World Heavyweight Championship</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> Galloway defended the championship in <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> for the first time on 20 March, defeating Andy Phoenix at Outback Championship Wrestling TV taping.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cagematch.net_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-cagematch.net-141">[141]</a></sup> Galloway made his first defense in Scotland as "World Champion" by defeating <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Joe_Coffey_(professional_wrestler)" title="Joe Coffey (professional wrestler)">Joe Coffey</a> in the main-event of BarraMania on 28 March. On 5 April, Galloway made his first defense of the ICW title in England defeating <a href="/wiki/Doug_Williams_(wrestler)" title="Doug Williams (wrestler)">Doug Williams</a> at a <a href="/wiki/Revolution_Pro_Wrestling" title="Revolution Pro Wrestling">Revolution Pro Wrestling</a> show<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> and on 6 April, Galloway made his first ICW title defense in Ireland at a Pro Wrestling Ulster show defeating <a href="/wiki/Joe_Hendry_(wrestler)" title="Joe Hendry (wrestler)">Joe Hendry</a>, TRON and Luther Valentine in a Four Way.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> On 11 April, Galloway defeated <a href="/wiki/Grado_(wrestler)" title="Grado (wrestler)">Grado</a> to retain the World Championship, after the match both men were attacked by returning former champion Jack Jester.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> The following night Galloway suffered his first loss in ICW since his return, teaming with Grado in a Tag Team match against Jester and <a href="/wiki/Sabu_(wrestler)" title="Sabu (wrestler)">Sabu</a>, where Grado was pinned.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> On 18 April, Galloway defeated both Jester and Grado in an impromptu triple threat match to retain his championship again, before having the championship stolen post-match by Sabu.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> The following night at "Alex Kidd In London" at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/KOKO_(venue)" title="KOKO (venue)">KOKO</a>, Galloway would regain possession of the belt and retain his championship in an Elimination Three Way Dance against Sabu and Jester.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> Galloway made his 13th successful World title defense by defeating <a href="/wiki/Tommy_End" title="Tommy End">Tommy End</a> on tour with ICW in Sheffield on 26 April 2015. Galloway finished the "Insane Entertainment Tour" by defeating Mikey Whiplash in the Main-Event of "Flawless Victory" on 2 May, to once again retain the ICW World Heavyweight Championship.</p>
<p>On 18 July, Galloway returned to New York to make his 15th successful title defence of the ICW World Heavyweight Championship, retaining the title in a Four-Way match against Joey Ace, Logan Black and Matt Macintosh at a Warriors of Wrestling show.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup></p>
<p>On October 16 at a Max Wrestling show in Germany, Galloway defended the ICW World Championship in a triple threat against Apu Singh and Chaos, in which Chaos' UEWA European Heavyweight Championship was also on the line.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup></p>
<p>At Shug's Hoose Party 2, Galloway turned heel along with Jack Jester and ICW GM Red Lightning as they aligned to form 'The Black Label'. With Jester's help he successfully defended the championship against Big Damo in the main event. Galloway would go on to successfully retain his World Championship against <a href="/wiki/Rhyno" title="Rhyno">Rhino</a>, Joey D and <a href="/wiki/Kris_Travis" title="Kris Travis">Kris Travis</a> throughout the rest of the summer.</p>
<p>As part of the "Road to Fear &amp; Loathing" tour, Galloway made successful title defenses of the ICW title against <a href="/wiki/Rampage_Brown" title="Rampage Brown">Rampage Brown</a>, Doug Williams, Matt Daly and Coach Trip, as well as non-title victories over <a href="/wiki/Rockstar_Spud" title="Rockstar Spud">Rockstar Spud</a>, Marty Scurll, Damo and <a href="/wiki/Kenny_Williams_(wrestler)" title="Kenny Williams (wrestler)">Kenny Williams</a>. During the tour, Galloway also teamed with Black Label stablemate Jack Jester to challenge Polo Promotions for the <a href="/wiki/ICW_Tag_Team_Championship" title="ICW Tag Team Championship">ICW Tag Team Championships</a> but were defeated following interference from Grado.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> On November 15, Galloway lost the title against Grado at <a href="/wiki/Fear_%26_Loathing_VIII" title="Fear &amp; Loathing VIII">Fear &amp; Loathing VIII</a>.</p>
<p>Galloway returned to ICW in February 2016 for the UK &amp; Ireland tour, scoring wins over Mark Coffey, Noam Dar and <a href="/wiki/BT_Gunn" title="BT Gunn">BT Gunn</a>, but suffering a loss in a match against Chris Renfrew for the ICW World Heavyweight Championship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceC_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceC-151">[151]</a></sup> Remaining in title contention, Galloway would lose two further ICW Championship matches against new world champion Big Damo in March and April.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceC_151-1"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceC-151">[151]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 29 May 2016, Galloway returned to winning ways in the main-event of the <a href="/wiki/Fight_Network" title="Fight Network">Fight Network</a> premiere episode of "ICW Friday Night Fight Club", teaming with Jester to defeat The Local Fire (Joe Hendry &amp; Davey Boy).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup></p>
<p>Galloway continued teaming with the Black Label in winning and losing efforts as well as scoring a singles victory over Grado in a rematch from Fear &amp; Loathing VIII.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> Galloway was then out of action from August until November due to a back injury but would appear on ICW shows in non-wrestling roles further his feud with Mark Dallas. On November 19, Galloway announced his departure from ICW due to the severity of his injuries, reconciling with Mark Dallas before attacking Dallas and revealing it to have been a rouse. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> Galloway then teamed with Jack Jester to defeat Chris Renfrew and Grado in an impromptu tag match.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup></p>
<p>Co-Main Eventing <a href="/wiki/Fear_%26_Loathing_IX" title="Fear &amp; Loathing IX">Fear &amp; Loathing IX</a>, Galloway and the rest of Team Black Label were defeated by Team Dallas in an Eight Man Elimination Tag Match for 100% ownership of ICW. Galloway was last eliminated by Renfrew following interference from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Finn_Balor" title="Finn Balor">Finn Balor</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Evolve_.282014.E2.80.93present.29">Evolve (2014–present)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Drew_Galloway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Evolve (2014–present)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 8 August 2014, in his first post-WWE match, Galloway debuted for <a href="/wiki/Evolve_(professional_wrestling)" title="Evolve (professional wrestling)">Evolve</a>, defeating <a href="/wiki/Chris_Hero" title="Chris Hero">Chris Hero</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Evolve_Championship" title="Evolve Championship">Evolve Championship</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Evolve31_157-0"><a href="#cite_note-Evolve31-157">[157]</a></sup> The next day, Galloway defeated Anthony Nese to retain the title.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup> His first loss in Evolve came at <i>Evolve 33</i>, in a Champion vs Champion match against the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DGUSA" title="DGUSA">DGUSA</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Open_The_Freedom_Gate" title="Open The Freedom Gate">Open the Freedom Gate</a> champion <a href="/wiki/Ricochet_(wrestler)" title="Ricochet (wrestler)">Ricochet</a>. Galloway continued to defend the Evolve championship stateside against the likes of Caleb Konley, <a href="/wiki/Stevie_Richards" title="Stevie Richards">Stevie Richards</a>, Devin Thomas, <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Rave" title="Jimmy Rave">Jimmy Rave</a> and Victor Sterling at Independent events across the US and <a href="/wiki/Rich_Swann" title="Rich Swann">Rich Swann</a> on Evolve iPPV at Evolve 34, while also defending the championship internationally in Scotland against Kid Fite, Johnny Moss, Big Damo and Andy Wild, as well as in England, where he retained by pinfall over reigning <a href="/wiki/NWA_World_Tag_Team_Championship" title="NWA World Tag Team Championship">NWA World Tag Team Champion</a> <a href="/wiki/David_Hart_Smith" title="David Hart Smith">Davey Boy Smith Jr</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following multiple international title defenses, Galloway renamed his title the "Evolve World Championship" on 9 January 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> Galloway made his first successful defense as World Champion the following night at Evolve 37, defeating Ricochet by pinfall.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup></p>
<p>The international title defenses continued on 20 March 2015, Galloway defeated Andy Phoenix in a Triple Championship match for Australian promotion Outback Championship Wrestling, retaining both the EVOLVE and ICW World Championships and winning Phoenix's OCW Heavyweight Championship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cagematch.net_141-1"><a href="#cite_note-cagematch.net-141">[141]</a></sup></p>
<p>Between 26 and 28 March 2015, Galloway competed on three of the WWN Wrestlemania week shows, at Evolve 39, Galloway retained the Evolve Championship over <a href="/wiki/Justin_Gabriel" title="Justin Gabriel">PJ Black</a> before a non-title victory over Uhaa Nation the following night at Evolve 40. On the third night, at Mercury Rising 2015, Galloway defeated <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Gargano" title="Johnny Gargano">Johnny Gargano</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Dragon_Gate_USA" title="Dragon Gate USA">Dragon Gate USA</a> <a href="/wiki/Open_the_Freedom_Gate_Championship" title="Open the Freedom Gate Championship">Open the Freedom Gate Championship</a> in a Title vs Title match, where he also retained the Evolve Championship to become Double Champion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MercuryRising2015_163-0"><a href="#cite_note-MercuryRising2015-163">[163]</a></sup></p>
<p>Galloway made a series of defenses of the Evolve and DGUSA titles between 4 and 6 April 2015 in Scotland, England and Northern Ireland, defeating <a href="/wiki/Marty_Scurll" title="Marty Scurll">Marty Scurll</a>, Doug Williams and Joe Hendry, Tron and Luther Valentine in a Four Way.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup></p>
<p>On May 30 at Evolve 43, Drew Galloway made his first standalone defense of the DGUSA Open the Freedom Gate championship, defeating <a href="/wiki/Biff_Busick" title="Biff Busick">Biff Busick</a> in the main-event via pinfall.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup> The following night at Evolve 44, Galloway defeated Roderick Strong to retain the Evolve title and end their feud.</p>
<p>On July 10, Galloway lost both the Evolve World Championship and the Open the Freedom Gate Championship to <a href="/wiki/Timothy_Thatcher" title="Timothy Thatcher">Timothy Thatcher</a>, at this point Galloway was the longest reigning Evolve champion in history and had set the record for most successful title defenses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> The following night at Evolve 46, Galloway stated that he had no issue <i>"starting from the bottom"</i> again and went on to defeat <a href="/wiki/Trent_Barreta" title="Trent Barreta">Trent Barreta</a> - following the match he was attacked by The Premiere Athlete Brand where he fended off the attack of Caleb Konley and Anthony Nese before uncharacteristically attacking <a href="/wiki/Betsy_Ruth" title="Betsy Ruth">Andrea</a>, threatening <a href="/wiki/SoCal_Val" title="SoCal Val">SoCal Val</a> and assaulting a referee. Following these actions Galloway showed remorse and retreated to the back. It was then announced that Galloway was suspended from EVOLVE.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following his suspension, Galloway returned to Evolve in November 2015 at Evolve 51, where he was victorious over <a href="/wiki/FIP_World_Heavyweight_Championship" title="FIP World Heavyweight Championship">FIP World Heavyweight Champion</a> Caleb Konley.
